`SimulatorConfig.adc_offset` | `adc_offset` | ADU | Integer output offset |\n    65â†’\n    66â†’## Critical Implicit Logic (pointer)\n    67â†’\n    68â†’Implicit pivot rules, beam-center mappings {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01CQJN7N4tKCUKgY7dqfQgYZ","type":"tool_result","content":"     1â†’# nanoBragg PyTorch Debugging Guidelines\n     2â†’\n     3â†’**Version:** 1.1  \n     4â†’**Date:** 2024-07-25  \n     5â†’**Owner:** PyTorch Development Team\n     6â†’\n     7â†’## Overview\n     8â†’\n     9â†’This document outlines the debugging methodology and tools for the nanoBragg PyTorch implementation. The debugging approach is built around a parallel trace comparison between the C code and the PyTorch implementation to ensure correctness and facilitate rapid issue resolution.\n    10â†’\n    11â†’## Core Debugging Philosophy\n    12â†’\n    13â†’### Parallel Trace Comparison Rule\n    14â†’\n    15â†’**CRITICAL:** All debugging of physics discrepancies MUST begin with a parallel trace comparison. This involves:\n    16â†’1. Generating a detailed, step-by-step log of intermediate variables from the original C code for a specific pixel (the \"Golden Trace\").\n    17â†’2. Generating an identical log from the PyTorch implementation using `scripts/debug_pixel_trace.py`.\n    18â†’3. Comparing these two logs line-by-line to find the first point of divergence.\n    19â†’\n    20â†’This methodology is mandatory to avoid guesswork and ensure bugs are found deterministically.\n    21â†’\n    22â†’## Debugging Workflow (SOP-4.1)\n    23â†’\n    24â†’Follow the specialized PyTorch physics debugging process documented in `docs/development/testing_strategy.md` (see the Parallel Validation Matrix section):\n    25â†’\n    26â†’1. **Identify an On-Peak Pixel:** Run the PyTorch simulation and visually inspect the output image to find the coordinates of a bright pixel on a Bragg peak.\n    27â†’2. **Generate Golden C Trace:** Add trace printf statements to `nanoBragg.c` around the calculation of interest (e.g., detector geometry, scattering vectors). Recompile with `make -C golden_suite_generator` and run with your test parameters, redirecting stderr to capture the trace log.\n    28â†’3. **Generate PyTorch Trace:** Create a debug script (e.g., `scripts/debug_beam_pivot_trace.py`) that replicates the exact calculation with matching trace output format.\n    29â†’4. **Compare Traces:** Use a diff tool (`diff`, `vimdiff`, etc.) to compare the C trace and the PyTorch trace.\n    30â†’5. **Identify Divergence Point:** Find the first variable where the numerical values differ significantly. This is the location of the bug.\n    31â†’6. **Isolate and Fix:** Examine the PyTorch code responsible for calculating the divergent variable. Check for common issues:\n    32â†’   - Unit conversion errors (e.g., meters vs. Angstroms).\n    33â†’   - Incorrect physical constants.\n    34â†’   - Mismatched mathematical formulas or conventions.\n    35â†’7. **Apply Fix and Re-validate:** Apply the fix and re-run the PyTorch trace. Repeat the comparison until the logs match.\n    36â†’\n    37â†’## Debug Script and Trace Management\n    38â†’\n    39â†’### Active PyTorch Debug Script\n    40â†’\n    41â†’**Script:** `scripts/debug_pixel_trace.py`  \n    42â†’**Purpose:** Generates the PyTorch side of the parallel trace comparison.\n    43â†’\n    44â†’### Golden C-Code Trace\n    45â†’\n    46â†’**Source:** Generated by adding printf statements to `nanoBragg.c` in `golden_suite_generator/`.  \n    47â†’**Example instrumentation:**\n    48â†’```c\n    49â†’/* Add trace output for detector geometry */\n    50â†’printf(\"TRACE_C: fdet_vector %.15g %.15g %.15g\\n\", fdet_vector[1], fdet_vector[2], fdet_vector[3]);\n    51â†’printf(\"TRACE_C: pix0_vector %.15g %.15g %.15g\\n\", pix0_vector[1], pix0_vector[2], pix0_vector[3]);\n    52â†’```\n    53â†’**Purpose:** Provides the \"ground truth\" intermediate values for the physics calculation.  \n    54â†’**Management:** Remove trace statements after debugging is complete to avoid cluttering output.\n    55â†’\n    56â†’### Trace Schema (names, units, precision)\n    57â†’\n    58â†’To ensure deterministic comparison between C and PyTorch traces, use the following conventions:\n    59â†’\n    60â†’- Prefixes: `TRACE_C:` for C-code; `TRACE_PY:` for PyTorch.\n    61â†’- Variable names: keep identical tokens across implementations (e.g., `pix0_vector`, `fdet_vector`, `sdet_vector`, `odet_vector`, `Fbeam`, `Sbeam`, `pixel_pos_meters`, `diffracted_vec`, `scattering_vec_A_inv`, `hkl_frac`, `F_cell`, `F_latt`, `omega_pixel`).\n    62â†’- Units:\n    63â†’  - Detector geometry and positions: meters (e.g., `pixel_pos_meters`, `pix0_vector`).\n    64â†’  - Physics quantities: Angstroms/Angstromâ»Â¹ as appropriate (e.g., wavelength in Ã…; scattering vector in Ã…â»Â¹).\n    65â†’- Precision: print with ~12â€“15 significant digits for numeric lines.\n    66â†’- One variable per line; consistent ordering between C and Py traces.\n    67â†’\n    68â†’## Key Variables to Compare\n    69â†’\n    70â†’When comparing traces, pay close attention to:\n    71â†’- **Scattering Vector q (or S):** The most common source of geometry errors.\n    72â†’- **Fractional Miller Index h,k,l:** Should be nearly identical.\n    73â†’- **F_latt:** Mismatches indicate errors in the crystal shape factor (sincg).\n    74â†’- **omega_pixel / polar:** Mismatches indicate errors in scaling factor calculations.\n    75â†’- **Final Intensity:** The final check for overall correctness.\n    76â†’\n    77â†’## Common Debugging Scenarios\n    78â†’\n    79â†’### Physics Calculation Issues\n    80â†’\n    81â†’**Symptoms:** Wrong intensity values, flat images, scale mismatches  \n    82â†’**First step:** Run pixel trace and compare scattering vector calculations  \n    83â†’**Common causes:** Missing 2Ï€ factors, unit conversion errors, coordinate transforms  \n    84â†’\n    85â†’### Unit System Problems\n    86â†’\n    87â†’**Symptoms:** Values off by powers of 10, dimension errors  \n    88â†’**First step:** Check pixel trace \"Additional Debugging Information\" section  \n    89â†’**Common causes:** Mixing Angstroms/meters, incorrect scaling factors  \n    90â†’\n    91â†’### Gradient Issues\n    92â†’\n    93â†’**Symptoms:** `torch.autograd.gradcheck` failures, \"modified in-place\" errors  \n    94â†’**First step:** Verify computation graph connectivity in trace  \n    95â†’**Common causes:** Manual tensor reassignment, detached operations\n    96â†’\n    97â†’### Gradient Flow Debugging\n    98â†’\n    99â†’**Symptoms:** `RuntimeError: element 0 of tensors does not require grad and does not have a grad_fn`  \n   100â†’**Methodology:** Use systematic isolation to find computation graph breaks:\n   101â†’\n   102â†’1. **Isolate the Problem:** Create minimal test case with `requires_grad=True` input\n   103â†’2. **Trace Through Computation:** Check `requires_grad` at each step\n   104â†’3. **Identify Break Point:** Find where `requires_grad` becomes `False`\n   105â†’4. **Common Causes:**\n   106â†’   - `.item()` calls on differentiable tensors (detaches from graph)\n   107â†’   - `torch.linspace` with tensor endpoints (known PyTorch limitation)\n   108â†’   - Manual tensor overwriting instead of functional computation\n   109â†’   - Using `.detach()` or `.numpy()` on tensors requiring gradients\n   110â†’\n   111â†’**Example Debug Pattern:**\n   112â†’```python\n   113â†’# Step 1: Isolate\n   114â†’phi_start = torch.tensor(10.0, requires_grad=True)\n   115â†’print(f\"phi_start requires_grad: {phi_start.requires_grad}\")\n   116â†’\n   117â†’# Step 2: Trace\n   118â†’config = CrystalConfig(phi_start_deg=phi_start)\n   119â†’print(f\"config.phi_start_deg requires_grad: {config.phi_start_deg.requires_grad}\")\n   120â†’\n   121â†’# Step 3: Identify break\n   122â†’if isinstance(config.phi_start_deg, float):\n   123â†’    print(\"ERROR: Gradient lost - tensor converted to float\")\n   124â†’```\n   125â†’\n   126â†’**Solutions:**\n   127â†’- Replace `.item()` with direct tensor passing\n   128â†’- Use manual tensor arithmetic instead of `torch.linspace`\n   129â†’- Enforce tensor inputs at architectural boundaries  \n   130â†’\n   131â†’### Coordinate System Issues\n   132â†’\n   133â†’**Symptoms:** 90-degree rotated images, incorrect peak positions  \n   134â†’**First step:** Verify pixel coordinate calculations in trace  \n   135â†’**Common causes:** `torch.meshgrid` indexing, axis orientation  \n   136â†’\n   137â†’## Debug Output Interpretation\n   138â†’\n   139â†’### Pixel Trace Log Structure\n   140â†’\n   141â†’```\n   142â†’================================================================================\n   143â†’Single Pixel Trace Debugging Log\n   144â†’nanoBragg PyTorch Implementation\n   145â†’================================================================================\n   146â†’\n   147â†’Target Pixel: (slow=100, fast=800)\n   148â†’Test Case: simple_cubic\n   149â†’Wavelength: 156â†’================================================================================\n   157â†’[Complete parameter dump]\n   158â†’```\n   159â†’\n   160â†’### Key Variables to Monitor\n   161â†’\n   162â†’- **Pixel Coordinate (Ã…):** Must be in Angstroms for physics calculations\n   163â†’- **Scattering Vector q (Ã…â»Â¹):** Critical for Miller index calculation\n   164â†’- **Fractional Miller Index h,k,l:** Should show spatial variation across detector\n   165â†’- **F_latt:** Shape factor - should vary significantly near Bragg peaks\n   166â†’- **Final Intensity:** Should match golden reference order of magnitude\n   167â†’\n   168â†’## Advanced Debugging\n   169â†’\n   170â†’### Memory and Performance Issues\n   171â†’\n   172â†’Use the existing debug scripts with smaller detector sizes:\n   173â†’```python\n   174â†’# Override detector size for debugging\n   175â†’detector_test.spixels = 3\n   176â†’detector_test.fpixels = 3\n   177â†’detector_test.invalidate_cache()\n   178â†’```\n   179â†’\n   180â†’### GPU vs CPU Differences\n   181â†’\n   182â†’Run identical calculations on both devices and compare intermediate values:\n   183â†’```python\n   184â†’# Compare device outputs\n   185â†’pytorch_image_cpu = simulator_cpu.run()\n   186â†’pytorch_image_gpu = simulator_gpu.run()\n   187â†’diff = torch.abs(pytorch_image_cpu - pytorch_image_gpu.cpu())\n   188â†’```\n   189â†’\n   190â†’### Precision Issues\n   191â†’\n   192â†’Use double precision for debugging:\n   193â†’```python\n   194â†’dtype = torch.float64  # Always use for debugging\n   195â†’# Check for precision loss in long calculation chains\n   196â†’```\n   197â†’\n   198â†’## Debug Script Maintenance\n   199â†’\n   200â†’### Updating the Active Script\n   201â†’\n   202â†’When modifying `scripts/debug_pixel_trace.py`:\n   203â†’1. this implementation uses Ã… for physics while keeping geometry in meters, with explicit conversions at the interface.\n    74â†’\n    75â†’- ADR-02 Rotation Order and Conventions\n    76â†’  - Basis initialization per convention (MOSFLM, XDS). Apply rotations in order: rotx â†’ roty â†’ rotz â†’ rotate around `twotheta_axis` by `detector_twotheta`.\n    77â†’  - Pivots: BEAM and SAMPLE formulas per spec.\n    78â†’\n    79â†’- ADR-03 Beam-center Mapping (MOSFLM) and +0.5 pixel Offsets\n    80â†’  - MOSFLM: Fbeam = Ybeam + 0.5Â·pixel; Sbeam = Xbeam + 0.5Â·pixel (after mmâ†’pixels). CUSTOM (when active): spec is silent; ADR decision is to not apply implicit +0.5 offsets unless provided by user inputs.\n    81â†’\n    82â†’- ADR-04 Pixel Coordinate Caching\n    83â†’  - Cache `get_pixel_coords()` outputs keyed implicitly by geometry version. Spec requires fixed defaults and -seed overrides. Implement the spec's LCG+shuffle PRNG for determinism; torch.Generator may be used only if it reproduces the exact bitstream.\n    87â†’\n    88â†’- ADR-08 Differentiability Preservation [CRITICAL]\n    89â†’  - All operations on differentiable parameters must maintain computation graph connectivity. See Section 15 for comprehensive guidelines.\n    90â†’  - Use @property methods for derived tensors, never overwrite with `.item()` or detached values.\n    91â†’  - Implement boundary enforcement: type conversions at call sites, tensor assumptions in core methods.\n    92â†’\n    93â†’- ADR-06 Interpolation Fallback [IMPLEMENTED]\n    94â†’  - Tricubic interpolation is enabled/disabled per spec. On out-of-range neighborhood, emit one-time warning, use default_F for that eval, and disable interpolation for the remainder of the run.\n    95â†’  - Implementation complete: `polint`/`polin2`/`polin3` in `utils/physics.py`, `_tricubic_interpolation` in `models/crystal.py`\n    96â†’  - Auto-enables for crystals with any dimension â‰¤ 2 cells\n    97â†’\n    98â†’- ADR-07 Oversample_* \"Last-value\" Semantics\n    99â†’  - When oversample_thick/polar/omega are NOT set, apply final capture/polarization/Î© once using the last computed value (loop-order dependent), matching the spec's caveat.\n   100â†’\n   101â†’- ADR-09 Detector Absorption Implementation [IMPLEMENTED]\n   102â†’  - Absorption parameters stored in DetectorConfig: `detector_abs_um` (attenuation depth), `detector_thick_um` (thickness), `detector_thicksteps` (layers)\n   103â†’  - Parallax factor Ï = dÂ·o computed per-pixel using detector normal and observation direction\n   104â†’  - Layer capture fractions: exp(âˆ’tÂ·Î”zÂ·Î¼/Ï) âˆ’ exp(âˆ’(t+1)Â·Î”zÂ·Î¼/Ï) where Î¼ = 1/attenuation_depth\n   105â†’\n   106â†’- ADR-10 Convention-Aware Incident Beam Direction [IMPLEMENTED]\n   107â†’  - beam along [0,0,1] (+Z axis)\n   110â†’  - Default to MOSFLM direction when no detector provided (for backward compatibility)\n   111â†’\n   112â†’- ADR-11 Full Tensor Vectorization [IMPLEMENTED 2025-09-24]\n   113â†’  - Eliminated all Python loops in core computation path for >10x performance gain\n   114â†’  - Subpixel sampling: Process all oversampleÃ—oversample subpixels as batch dimension (S, F, oversampleÂ²)\n   115â†’  - Thickness layers: Process all detector layers in parallel using broadcasting (thicksteps, S, F)\n   116â†’  - Maintains exact numerical equivalence with loop-based implementation\n   117â†’  - Enables efficient GPU acceleration through pure tensor operations\n   118â†’\n   119â†’- ADR-12 Golden Data Generation Strategy [2025-09-24]\n   120â†’  - - Accept minor numerical tolerance differences (â‰¤0.001 correlation) between C and PyTorch implementations\n   123â†’  - Document exact generation commands in tests/golden_data/README.md for reproducibility\n   124â†’\n   125â†’## 3) Highâ€‘Level System Architecture\n   126â†’\n   127â†’- CLI & Config Layer [IMPLEMENTED]\n   128â†’  - `__main__.py` - Entry point with argparse, maps CLI 144â†’## 4) Module Structure [IMPLEMENTED]\n   145â†’\n   146â†’```\n   147â†’nanobrag_torch/\n   148â†’  config.py                # DetectorConfig, CrystalConfig, BeamConfig (+ enums)\n   149â†’ Parse CLI and headers [IMPLEMENTED], resolve precedence; build CrystalConfig, DetectorConfig, BeamConfig.\n   205â†’2. Instantiate Detector (meters) and Crystal (Ã…). Optionally load HKL or Fdump.\n   206â†’3. Compute `pix0_vector` per pivot and convention; compute basis rotations; cache pixel coords in meters, convert to Ã… for physics.\n   207â†’4. Build sampling sets: phi (phi_steps), mosaic (mosaic_domains), sources (divergence/dispersion), subpixels (oversample^2), thickness steps.\n   208â†’5. For each pixel/subpixel/thickness/source/phi/mosaic:\n   209â†’   - pos = D0 + FdetÂ·f + SdetÂ·s (+ OdetÂ·o if thick); d = unit(pos); R=|pos|; Î© = pixel^2/R^2Â·(close_distance/R) or 1/R^2 if point-pixel.\n   210â†’   - i = âˆ’source_dir; Î» from source; q = (dâˆ’i)/Î»; stol=0.5Â·|q|; cull if dmin>0 and stol>0 and dmin>0.5/stol.\n   211â†’   - Rotate (a,b,c) by phi about spindle; apply mosaic rotation; compute h=aÂ·q, k=bÂ·q, l=cÂ·q.\n   212â†’   - h0,k0,l0 = ceil(xâˆ’0.5) (nearest int); F_latt via selected lattice model.\n   213â†’   - F_cell via tricubic (if enabled and in-bounds) else nearest or default_F per spec fallback.\n   214â†’   - Polarization per Kahn model unless -nopolar.\n   215â†’   - Accumulate I_term = (F_cell^2)Â·(F_latt^2) with oversample_* caveats (last-value vs per-term multiply).\n   216â†’6. Final scaling per pixel: S = r_e^2 Â· fluence Â· I / steps; if oversample_* toggles are off, multiply S once by the last computed capture/polarization/Î© per spec. Add background I_bg if enabled. Write outputs.\n   217â†’\n   218â†’## 7) Geometry Model & Conventions\n   219â†’\n   220â†’- Basis vectors and defaults (initial, before rotations):\n   221â†’  - ADXV:   f=[1,0,0], s=[0,âˆ’1,0], o=[0,0,1],  beam=[0,0,1], default twotheta_axis=[âˆ’1,0,0]; pivot=BEAM. Default beam centers: Xbeam=(detsize_f+pixel)/2, Ybeam=(detsize_sâˆ’pixel)/2; mapping Fbeam=Xbeam, Sbeam=detsize_sâˆ’Ybeam.\n   222â†’  - MOSFLM: f=[0,0,1], s=[0,âˆ’1,0], o=[1,0,0],  beam=[1,0,0], default twotheta_axis=[0,0,âˆ’1]; pivot=BEAM. Beam-center mapping: Fbeam=Xbeam; Sbeam=Ybeam (defaults Xbeam=Xclose, Ybeam=Yclose).\n   225â†’  - DIALS:  f=[1,0,0], s=[0,1,0],  o=[0,0,1],  beam=[0,0,1], default twotheta_axis=[0,1,0];  pivot=SAMPLE. Beam-center mapping: Fbeam=Xbeam; Sbeam=Ybeam.\n   226â†’- Rotations: apply XYZ small-angle rotations to f/s/o, then rotate around twotheta_axis by two-theta.\n   227â†’- r-factor update: r = bÂ·o_after; if close_distance unspecified: close_distance = |rÂ·distance|; then set distance = close_distance / r. Direct-beam Fbeam/Sbeam recomputed from R = close_distance/rÂ·b âˆ’ D0.\n   228â†’- Pivots:\n   229â†’  - SAMPLE: D0 = âˆ’FcloseÂ·f âˆ’ ScloseÂ·s + close_distanceÂ·o, then rotate D0 (pix0) with detector rotations and two-theta.\n   230â†’  - BEAM: D0 = âˆ’FbeamÂ·f âˆ’ SbeamÂ·s + distanceÂ·beam (after rotations); preserves beam center.\n   231â†’  - CLI forcing and precedence (per spec-a):\n   232â†’    - Providing `-distance` (without `-close_distance`) forces BEAM pivot; providing `-close_distance` forces SAMPLE pivot.\n   233â†’    - Providing beam-center style inputs forces pivot: `-Xbeam`/`-Ybeam` â†’ BEAM; `-Xclose`/`-Yclose` or `-ORGX`/`-ORGY` â†’ SAMPLE.\n   234â†’    - Explicit `-pivot` overrides either.\n   235â†’- Beam center mapping:\n   236â†’  - ADXV:   Fbeam = Xbeam; Sbeam = detsize_s âˆ’ Ybeam.\n   237â†’  - MOSFLM: Fbeam = Ybeam + 0.5Â·pixel; Sbeam = Xbeam + 0.5Â·pixel (mmâ†’pixelsâ†’meters).\n   238â†’  - DENZO:  Fbeam = Ybeam; Sbeam = Xbeam.\n   239â†’  - XDS/DIALS: Fbeam = Xbeam; Sbeam = Ybeam.\n   240â†’  - CUSTOM: spec is silent; ADR decision is to not apply implicit +0.5 offsets unless provided by user inputs.\n   241â†’- Curved detector [IMPLEMENTED]: spherical mapping via small-angle rotations Sdet/distance and Fdet/distance.\n   242â†’\n   243â†’## 8) Physics Model & Scaling\n   244â†’\n   245â†’- Scattering vector and stol: i = âˆ’source_dir (unit), d=unit(pos), q=(dâˆ’i)/Î» [mâˆ’1 in spec; Angstroms in implementation], stol=0.5Â·|q|.\n   246â†’- Lattice shape models:\n   247â†’  - SQUARE: F_latt = sincg(Ï€Â·h,Na) Â· sincg(Ï€Â·k,Nb) Â· sincg(Ï€Â·l,Nc).\n   248â†’  - ROUND:  F_latt = NaÂ·NbÂ·NcÂ·0.723601254558268 Â· sinc3(Ï€Â·sqrt(fudgeÂ·hrad^2)).\n   249â†’  - GAUSS/TOPHAT: per spec formulas using Î”r*^2 and cutoff.\n   250â†’- Structure factors: tricubic 4Ã—4Ã—4 interpolation with fallback; nearest-neighbor otherwise; default_F out-of-range.\n   251â†’- Polarization (Kahn): factor = 0.5Â·(1 + cos^2(2Î¸) âˆ’ KÂ·cos(2Ïˆ)Â·sin^2(2Î¸)), Ïˆ from EB-plane projection.\n   252â†’- Absorption & parallax: per-layer capture fraction = exp(âˆ’tÂ·Î”zÂ·Î¼/Ï) âˆ’ exp(âˆ’(t+1)Â·Î”zÂ·Î¼/Ï), Ï=dÂ·o.\n   253â†’- Solid angle: Î© = pixel^2/R^2 Â· (close_distance/R); point-pixel: Î© = 1/R^2.\n   254â†’- Background: I_bg = (F_bg^2)Â·r_e^2Â·fluenceÂ·(water_size^3)Â·1e6Â·Avogadro/18.\n   255â†’- Steps normalization: steps = sourcesÂ·mosaic_domainsÂ·phistepsÂ·oversample^2; S = r_e^2Â·fluenceÂ·I/steps; apply last-value factors if oversample_* toggles are off.\n   256â†’\n   257â†’## 9) HKL Data & Interpolation\n   258â†’\n   259â†’- Text HKL read: two-pass min/max then grid allocations; non-integer warnings; unspecified points initialized to default_F when requested.\n   260â†’- Binary Fdump: header of six ints, form-feed separator, then (h_range+1)Ã—(k_range+1)Ã—(l_range+1) doubles in native endianness (fastest-varying l).\n   261â†’- Interpolation: enable/disable via flags; auto-enable if any of Na/Nb/Nc â‰¤ 2 (per spec defaults) unless user forces off.\n   262â†’\n   263â†’## 10) I/O â€” Headers & Image Files [IMPLEMENTED]\n   264â†’\n   265â†’- SMV integer images:\n   266â†’  - Header keys exactly as spec; close with `}\\f`; pad to 512 bytes; data unsigned short, slow-major ordering (fast index contiguous; pixel index = slow*fpixels + fast).\n   267â†’  - Scale factor: if â‰¤0 or missing, set to 55000/max(float) else 1.0; add ADC offset (default 40), clip [0,65535].\n   268â†’- Noise images:\n   269â†’  - Poisson (exact <12, rejection up to 1e6, Gaussian approx >1e6), then ADC and clipping; overload count tracked.\n   270â†’- PGM:\n   271â†’  - P5 with comment line `# pixels scaled by <pgm_scale>`; values floor(min(255, float_pixel * pgm_scale)).\n   272â†’- Header ingestion from -img/-mask: recognized keys applied; last file read wins; for -mask, Y beam center interpreted as detsize_s âˆ’ value_mm.\n   273â†’\n   274â†’## 11) RNG & Seeds [IMPLEMENTED]\n   275â†’\n   276â†’- Domains and defaults:\n   277â†’  - noise_seed = negative wall-clock time (spec default), override via -seed.\n   278â†’  - mosaic_seed = âˆ’12345678 (spec default) unless set.\n   279â†’  - misset_seed = noise_seed unless set.\n   280â†’- PRNG: Implement the specâ€™s linear congruential generator with shuffle table for all RNG domains to guarantee deterministic, cross-device reproducibility. Torch generators may be used for performance only if they reproduce the identical bitstream; otherwise, use the custom PRNG directly.\n   281â†’\n   282â†’## 12) Testing Strategy (maps to spec Acceptance Tests)\n   283â†’\n   284â†’- Unit tests\n   285â†’  - geometry: basis vectors per convention, pix0, r-factor distance update, Î© calculation, point-pixel.\n   286â†’  - crystal: triclinic tensors, misset rotation, phi/mosaic rotations.\n   287â†’  - physics: sincg numerical stability, polarization factor, absorption layers, steps normalization.\n   288â†’  - io: SMV header serialization, Fdump read/write, PGM writer.\n   289â†’\n   290â†’- Integration tests\n   291â†’  - Acceptance Tests from specs/spec-a.md (â€œAcceptance Tests (Normative)â€), including AT-GEO-001..AT-STA-001.\n   292â†’  - C-vs-PyTorch trace parity for selected pixels (debug scripts).\n   293â†’\n   294â†’## 13) Implementation Plan (incremental)\n   295â†’\n   296â†’1) Geometry correctness\n   297â†’  - Fix MOSFLM BEAM-pivot beam-center mapping; add r-factor distance update; align default pivots per spec.\n   298â†’2) Steps normalization & Î© last-value caveat\n   299â†’  - Implement steps division; wire oversample_* toggles with last-value behavior.\n   300â†’3) Absorption & thickness\n   301â†’  - Implement per-layer capture fractions and -oversample_thick semantics.\n   302â†’4) Polarization\n   303â†’  - Implement Kahn model; Precision-critical operations (gradient checks, metric duality validation) override to float64 explicitly where required.\n   314â†’- device: CPU default; opt-in CUDA via `.to(device)`.\n   315â†’- Tolerances: geometry comparisons use atol ~1e-15 for cached basis checks (with float64); acceptance checks use explicit tolerances per test appropriate for float32 precision.\n   316â†’- When spec and C disagree subtly on rounding, use spec's rounding: nearest integer via `ceil(x âˆ’ 0.5)`.\n   317â†’\n   318â†’## 15) Differentiability Guidelines (Critical for PyTorch Implementation)\n   319â†’\n   320â†’### Core Principles\n   321â†’\n   322â†’The PyTorch implementation **MUST** maintain end-to-end differentiability to enable gradient-based optimization. This is a fundamental architectural requirement that affects every design decision.\n   323â†’\n   324â†’### Mandatory Rules\n   325â†’\n   326â†’1. **Never Use `.item()` on Differentiable Tensors**\n   327â†’   - **Forbidden:** `config = Config(param=tensor.item())` â€” permanently severs computation graph\n   328â†’   - **Correct:** `config = Config(param=tensor)` â€” preserves gradient flow\n   329â†’   - **Rationale:** `.item()` extracts a Python scalar, completely detaching from autograd\n   330â†’\n   331â†’2. **Avoid `torch.linspace` for Gradient-Critical Code**\n   332â†’   - **Problem:** `torch.linspace` doesn't preserve gradients from tensor endpoints\n   333â†’   - **Forbidden:** `torch.linspace(start_tensor, end_tensor, steps)` where tensors require gradients\n   334â†’   - **Correct:** `start_tensor + (end_tensor - start_tensor) * torch.arange(steps) / (steps - 1)`\n   335â†’   - **Alternative:** Use manual tensor arithmetic for all range generation needing gradients\n   336â†’\n   337â†’3. **Implement Derived Properties as Functions**\n   338â†’   - **Forbidden:** Overwriting class attributes with computed values (e.g., `self.a_star = calculate_reciprocal()`)\n   339â†’   - **Correct:** Use `@property` decorators that recalculate from base parameters each access\n   340â†’   - **Example:** Crystal reciprocal vectors must be computed from cell parameters on-demand\n   341â†’\n   342â†’4. **Boundary Enforcement for Type Safety**\n   343â†’   - **Pattern:** Core methods assume tensor inputs; handle type conversions at call sites only\n   344â†’   - **Forbidden:** `isinstance(param, torch.Tensor)` checks inside computational methods\n   345â†’   - **Correct:** Convert scalars to tensors at API boundaries, maintain tensors throughout core\n   346â†’   - **Benefit:** Clean architecture while preserving gradient flow\n   347â†’\n   348â†’5. **Avoid Gradient-Breaking Operations**\n   349â†’   - **Forbidden in gradient paths:**\n   350â†’     - `.detach()` â€” explicitly breaks gradient connection\n   351â†’     - `.numpy()` â€” converts to NumPy array, losing autograd\n   352â†’     - `.cpu()` without maintaining graph â€” can break device consistency\n   353â†’   - **Allowed:** These operations are safe in non-differentiable contexts (logging, visualization)\n   354â†’\n   355â†’### Testing Requirements\n   356â†’\n   357â†’**Every differentiable parameter MUST have:**\n   358â†’1. **Unit-level gradient test:** Verify gradients flow through isolated functions\n   359â†’2. **Integration gradient test:** Verify end-to-end gradient flow through complete simulation\n   360â†’3. **Stability test:** Verify gradients remain stable across parameter variations\n   361â†’4. **Use `torch.autograd.gradcheck`:** With `dtype=torch.float64` for numerical precision (note: gradient tests explicitly override to float64 for accuracy, even though default dtype is float32)\n   362â†’\n   363â†’### Common Pitfalls and Solutions\n   364â†’\n   365â†’| Pitfall | Symptom | Solution |\n   366â†’|---------|---------|----------|\n   367â†’| Using `.item()` in config | Gradients are None | Pass tensors directly |\n   368â†’| `torch.linspace` with tensor bounds | No gradient on start/end | Manual arithmetic |\n   369â†’| Overwriting derived attributes | Stale gradients | Use @property methods |\n   370â†’| Type checks in core methods | Complex branching | Boundary enforcement |\n   371â†’| In-place operations | Runtime errors | Use out-of-place ops |\n   372â†’\n   373â†’### Architecture Implications\n   374â†’\n   375â†’- **Config objects:** Must accept both scalars and tensors, preserving tensor types\n   376â†’- **Model classes:** Use @property for all derived geometric/crystallographic quantities\n   377â†’- **Simulator:** Maintain tensor operations throughout; batch operations for efficiency\n   378â†’- **Utils:** Implement gradient-safe versions of standard operations (ranges, interpolation)\n   379â†’\n   380â†’### Debugging Gradient Issues\n   381â†’\n   382â†’1. **Check requires_grad:** Verify input tensors have `requires_grad=True`\n   383â†’2. **Print computation graph:** Use `torchviz` or `tensorboard` to visualize graph\n   384â†’3. **Isolate breaks:** Binary search through operations to find where gradients stop\n   385â†’4. **Use retain_graph:** For debugging multiple backward passes\n   386â†’5. **Check autograd.grad:** Manually compute gradients for specific tensors\n   387â†’\n   388â†’### Reference Documentation\n   389â†’\n   390â†’For comprehensive details and examples:\n   391â†’- **Lessons learned:** `docs/development/lessons_in_differentiability.md` â€” real debugging cases and solutions\n   392â†’- **Design principles:** `docs/architecture/pytorch_design.md` â€” architectural patterns for differentiability\n   393â†’- **Testing strategy:** `docs/development/testing_strategy.md` â€” Tier 2 gradient correctness methodology\n   394â†’- **Parameter trace:** `docs/architecture/parameter_trace_analysis.md` â€” understanding gradient flow paths\n   395â†’\n   396â†’### Verification Checklist\n   397â†’\n   398â†’- [ ] All `.item()` calls verified as non-differentiable paths\n   399â†’- [ ] No `torch.linspace` with gradient-requiring endpoints\n   400â†’- [ ] All derived properties use @property or functional patterns\n   401â†’- [ ] Type conversions happen only at boundaries\n   402â†’- [ ] `torch.autograd.gradcheck` passes for all parameters\n   403â†’- [ ] Integration tests verify end-to-end gradient flow\n   404â†’\n   405â†’**Remember:** Breaking differentiability breaks the fundamental value proposition of the PyTorch port â€” the ability to optimize physical parameters via gradient descent.\n   406â†’\n   407â†’## 16) Developer Notes\n   408â†’\n   409â†’- Maintain strict separation between geometry (meters) and physics (Ã…). Convert once at the interface.\n   410â†’- **Preserve differentiability at all costs:** Follow Section 15 guidelines religiously. Use Python-level control flow (like `isinstance`) to handle different input types gracefully, but ensure the core operations are performed on tensors.\n   129â†’    -   **Known Limitation:** Be aware that some PyTorch functions, like `torch.linspace`, do not propagate gradients to their `start` and `end` arguments. In such cases, a manual, differentiable implementation using basic tensor operations (e.g., `torch.arange`) is required.\n   130â†’    -   **Verification:** All differentiable parameters must have passing `torch.autograd.gradcheck` tests.\n   131â†’\n   132â†’8.  **Preserve C-Code References Until Feature-Complete:** C-code quotes in docstrings serve as a roadmap for unimplemented features. They **MUST NOT** be removed until the corresponding feature is fully implemented, tested, and validated.\n   133â†’    -   **Action:** When implementing a feature described by a C-code quote, leave the quote in place. Once the feature is complete and all its tests (including integration and gradient tests) are passing, the quote may be updated or removed if it no longer adds value beyond the implemented code.\n   134â†’    -   **Example:** A docstring for an unimplemented function should retain its C-code reference. A docstring for a partially implemented function (e.g., `phi` rotation is done but `misset` is not) should retain the C-code reference for the unimplemented part, clearly marked as \"Future Work\".\n   135â†’    -   **Verification:** Before removing any C-code reference, confirm that the functionality it describes is covered by a passing test in the test suite.\n   136â†’\n   137â†’9.  **Never Use `.item()` on Differentiable Tensors:** The `.item()` method **MUST NOT** be used on any tensor that needs to remain differentiable.\n   138â†’    -   **Action:** Pass tensors directly to configuration objects and functions instead of extracting scalar values.\n   139â†’    -   **Forbidden:** `config = Config(param=tensor.item())` - This permanently severs the computation graph.\n   140â†’    -   **Correct:** `config = Config(param=tensor)` - Preserves gradient flow.\n   141â†’    -   **Verification:** Any use of `.item()` must be followed by verification that the tensor is not needed for gradient computation.\n   142â†’\n   143â†’9.  **Avoid `torch.linspace` for Gradient-Critical Code:** `torch.linspace` does not preserve gradients from tensor endpoints.\n   144â†’    -   **Action:** Use manual tensor arithmetic for differentiable range generation: `start + step_size * torch.arange(...)`.\n   145â†’    -   **Forbidden:** `torch.linspace(start_tensor, end_tensor, steps)` where `start_tensor` or `end_tensor` require gradients.\n   146â†’    -   **Correct:** `start_tensor + (end_tensor - start_tensor) * torch.arange(steps) / (steps - 1)`.\n   147â†’    -   **Verification:** Check that generated ranges preserve `requires_grad=True` when input tensors require gradients.\n   148â†’\n   149â†’10. **Boundary Enforcement for Type Safety:** Use clean architectural boundaries to handle tensor/scalar conversions.\n   150â†’    -   **Action:** Core methods assume tensor inputs; Failure to include this reference is considered an implementation error.\n   181â†’\n   182â†’12. **Critical Data Flow Convention: The Misset Rotation Pipeline**\n   183â†’\n   184â†’    **This rule is non-negotiable and describes a non-standard data flow that MUST be replicated exactly.** The static misset orientation is integrated into the lattice vector calculation in a specific sequence.\n   185â†’\n   186â†’    The correct, end-to-end data flow is:\n   187â†’    1.  Calculate the **base** real (`a,b,c`) and reciprocal (`a*,b*,c*`) vectors from the six unit cell parameters in a canonical orientation.\n   188â†’    2.  Apply the static misset rotation matrix to **only the reciprocal vectors** (`a*,b*,c*`).\n   189â†’    3.  **Crucially, recalculate the real-space vectors (`a,b,c`) from the newly rotated reciprocal vectors** using the standard crystallographic relationship (e.g., `a = (b* x c*) * V`).\n   190â†’    4.  These recalculated, misset-aware real-space vectors are then passed to the dynamic rotation pipeline (`get_rotated_real_vectors`) and are ultimately used in the simulator's Miller index calculation (`h = SÂ·a`).\n   191â†’\n   192â†’    **Rationale:** This specific sequence is how `nanoBragg.c` ensures the static orientation is correctly propagated. Any deviation will cause the simulation to fail validation against the golden test cases.\n   193â†’\n   194â†’13. **Reciprocal Vector Recalculation for Self-Consistency**\n   195â†’\n   196â†’    **The C-code performs a circular recalculation that MUST be replicated for exact metric duality.** After building initial reciprocal vectors and calculating real vectors from them, the C-code recalculates the reciprocal vectors using the standard formula.\n   197â†’\n   198â†’    The complete sequence is:\n   199â†’    1. Build initial reciprocal vectors using the default orientation convention\n   200â†’    2. Calculate real vectors from reciprocal: `a = (b* Ã— c*) Ã— V`\n   201â†’    3. **Recalculate reciprocal vectors from real**: `a* = (b Ã— c) / V_actual`\n   202â†’    4. **Use actual volume**: `V_actual = a Â· (b Ã— c)` instead of the formula volume\n   203â†’\n   204â†’    **Critical:** The volume from the actual vectors differs slightly (~0.6% for triclinic cells) from the formula volume. Using V_actual ensures perfect metric duality (aÂ·a* = 1 exactly).\n   205â†’\n   206â†’    **Verification:** The `test_metric_duality` test must pass with `rtol=1e-12`.\n   207â†’\n   208â†’14. **Mandatory Component Contracts:** For any non-trivial component port (e.g., `Detector`, `Crystal`), the first step of the implementation phase **MUST** be to author (or consult, if it exists) a complete technical specification in `docs/architecture/[component_name].md`. This is equivalent to the `|Q| = 2Ï€/d` convention where `Q = 2Ï€G`. All tests and calculations must be consistent with this standard.\n   234â†’\n   235â†’**Default Orientation Matrix**: The project uses the nanoBragg.c convention for constructing the default orientation of reciprocal lattice vectors from cell parameters:\n   236â†’- a* is placed purely along the x-axis\n   237â†’- b* is placed in the x-y plane  \n   238â†’- c* fills out 3D space\n   239â†’\n   240â†’This specific orientation must be maintained for consistency with the C-code implementation.\n   241â†’\n   242â†’## Golden Test Case Specification (`simple_cubic`)\n   243â†’\n   244â†’**The exact `nanoBragg.c` commands used to generate all golden reference data are centrally documented in `tests/golden_data/README.md`. The codebase consists of:\n   260â†’\n   261â†’- **Core C simulators**: `nanoBragg.c` (main diffraction simulator), `nonBragg.c` (amorphous scattering), `noisify.c` (noise addition)\n   262â†’- **PyTorch port documentation**: Complete architectural design and implementation plan in `./docs/`\n   263â†’- **Auxiliary tools**: Shell scripts for data conversion and matrix generation\n   264â†’\n   265â†’## Build Commands\n   266â†’\n   267â†’### C Code Compilation\n   268â†’```bash\n   269â†’# Standard build\n   270â†’gcc -O3 -o nanoBragg nanoBragg.c -lm -fopenmp\n   271â†’\n   272â†’# Build other simulators\n   273â†’gcc -O3 -o nonBragg nonBragg.c -lm\n   274â†’gcc -O3 -o noisify noisify.c -lm\n   275â†’```\n   276â†’\n   277â†’### Binaries and Instrumentation (IMPORTANT)\n   278â†’- Treat the root `./nanoBragg` as a frozen reference binary; do not rebuild it for tracing.\n   279â†’- Build and recompile any instrumented C binary under `golden_suite_generator/` (e.g., `./golden_suite_generator/nanoBragg`).\n   280â†’- Always invoke the C runner via `NB_C_BIN`:\n   281â†’  - Recommended: `export NB_C_BIN=./golden_suite_generator/nanoBragg`\n   282â†’  - Alternative: `export NB_C_BIN=./nanoBragg`\n   283â†’- Tooling (e.g., comparison scripts) SHOULD resolve the C runner in this order:\n   284â†’  1) `--c-bin` arg if provided\n   285â†’  2) `NB_C_BIN` env var\n   286â†’  3) `./golden_suite_generator/nanoBragg` if present\n   287â†’  4) `./nanoBragg`\n   288â†’  5) Otherwise, error with guidance\n   289â†’\n   290â†’### No Testing Framework\n   291â†’The repository currently uses manual validation through example runs and visual inspection. No automated test suite exists for the C code.\n   292â†’\n   293â†’## Core Architecture\n   294â†’\n   295â†’### C Implementation Structure\n   296â†’- **Single-file architecture**: All core logic in `nanoBragg.c` (~49k lines)\n   297â†’- **Procedural design**: Sequential execution through main() function\n   298â†’- **Three-phase execution**:\n   299â†’  1. **Setup Phase**: Parse arguments, load files, initialize geometry\n   300â†’  2. **Simulation Loop**: Nested loops over pixels, sources, mosaic domains, phi steps\n   301â†’  3. **Output Phase**: Apply scaling, add noise, write image files\n   302â†’\n   303â†’### Key Data Flow\n   304â†’1. **Input**: Structure factors (HKL file), crystal orientation (matrix file), beam/detector parameters\n   305â†’2. **Core calculation**: For each detector pixel, sum contributions from all source points, mosaic domains, and phi steps\n   306â†’3. **Output**: SMV-format diffraction images with optional noise\n   307â†’\n   308â†’### OpenMP Parallelization\n   309â†’- Single `#pragma omp parallel for` directive on outer pixel loop\n   310â†’- Shared read-only data (geometry, structure factors)\n   311â†’- Private per-thread variables for calculations\n   312â†’- Reduction clauses for global statistics\n   313â†’\n   314â†’## PyTorch Port Design\n   315â†’\n   316â†’The `./docs/` directory contains a complete architectural design for a PyTorch reimplementation:\n   317â†’\n   318â†’### Key Design Principles\n   319â†’- **Vectorization over loops**: Replace nested C loops with broadcasting tensor operations\n   320â†’- **Object-oriented structure**: `Crystal`, `Detector`, `Simulator` classes\n   321â†’- **Differentiable parameters**: Enable gradient-based optimization. **(See Core Implementation Rules above)**\n   322â†’- **GPU acceleration**: Leverage PyTorch's CUDA backend\n   323â†’- **Consistent Units**: All internal calculations use Angstroms. **(See Core Implementation Rules above)**\n   324â†’\n Introduction & Philosophy\n     8â†’\n     9â†’This document outlines the comprehensive testing strategy for the PyTorch implementation of nanoBragg. The primary goal is to ensure that the new application is a correct, verifiable, and trustworthy scientific tool.\n    10â†’Our testing philosophy is a three-tiered hybrid approach, designed to build confidence layer by layer:\n    11â†’\n    12â†’1. **Tier 1: Translation Correctness:** We first prove that the PyTorch code is a faithful, numerically precise reimplementation of the original C code's physical model. The C code is treated as the \"ground truth\" specification.\n    13â†’2. **Tier 2: Gradient Correctness:** We then prove that the new differentiable capabilities are mathematically sound.\n    14â†’3. **Tier 3: Scientific Validation:** Finally, we validate the model against objective physical principles.\n    15â†’\n    16â†’All tests will be implemented using the PyTest framework.\n    17â†’\n    18â†’### 1.4 PyTorch Device & Dtype Discipline\n    19â†’\n    20â†’- **Device-neutral code:** Every PyTorch path MUST operate correctly on both CPU and CUDA tensors and across supported dtypes. Do not hard-code `.cpu()`/`.cuda()` calls, create CPU-only constants, or assume float64 execution when the caller may supply float32/half tensors.\n    21â†’- **Authoritative smoke runs:** When a change touches tensor math, run the authoritative reproduction command once on CPU and once on CUDA (when available). Capture both logs/metrics and attach them to the fix plan. Treat any `torch.compile` or Dynamo warning about mixed devices as blocking.\n    22â†’- **Targeted tests:** Prefer parametrised tests that iterate over `device in {\"cpu\", \"cuda\"}` (guarded by `torch.cuda.is_available()`). At minimum, ensure a `gpu_smoke` marker or equivalent pytest node exercises the new logic on CUDA before declaring success.\n    23â†’- **Helper utilities:** Encapsulate device/dtype harmonisation in small helpers (e.g., `tensor.to(other_tensor)` or `type_as`). Centralise these helpers in reusable modules to keep the rule enforceable across future PyTorch projects.\n    24â†’- **CI gate:** If CI offers GPU runners, add a fast smoke job that runs the `gpu_smoke` marker (or agreed command) so regressions like CPUâ†”GPU tensor mixing fail quickly.\n    25â†’- **Vectorization check:** Confirm `_compute_physics_for_position` and related helpers remain batched across sources/phi/mosaic/oversample; extend broadcast dimensions instead of adding Python loops.\n    26â†’- **Runtime checklist:** Consult `docs/development/pytorch_runtime_checklist.md` during development and cite it in fix-plan notes for PyTorch changes.\n    27â†’\n    28â†’## 2. Configuration Parity\n    29â†’\n    30â†’**CRITICAL REQUIREMENT:** Before implementing any test that compares against C-code output, you **MUST** ensure exact configuration parity. All golden test cases must be generated with commands that are verifiably equivalent to the PyTorch test configurations.\n    31â†’\n    32â†’**Authoritative Reference:** See the **[C-CLI to PyTorch Configuration Map](./c_to_pytorch_config_map.md)** for:\n    33â†’- Complete parameter mappings\n    34â†’- Implicit conventions (pivot modes, beam adjustments, rotation axes)\n    35â†’- Common configuration bugs and prevention strategies\n    36â†’\n    37â†’Configuration mismatches are the most common source of test failures. Always verify:\n    38â†’- Pivot mode (BEAM vs SAMPLE) based on parameter implications\n    39â†’- Convention-specific adjustments (e.g., MOSFLM's 0.5 pixel offset)\n    40â†’- Default rotation axes for each convention\n    41â†’- Proper unit conversions at boundaries\n    42â†’ - Explicit convention selection: tests and harnesses MUST pass `-convention` (or equivalent API flag) to avoid implicit CUSTOM switching when vector parameters are present\n    43â†’\n    44â†’\n    45â†’## 2.1 Ground Truth: Parallel Trace-Driven Validation\n    46â†’\n    47â†’The foundation of our testing strategy is a \"Golden Suite\" of test data. Crucially, final-output comparison is insufficient for effective debugging. Our strategy is therefore centered on **Parallel Trace-Driven Validation**.\n    48â†’\n    49â†’For each test case, the Golden Suite must contain three components:\n    50â†’1. **Golden Output Image:** The final .bin file from the C code.\n    51â†’2. **Golden C-Code Trace Log:** A detailed, step-by-step log of intermediate variables from the C code for a specific on-peak pixel.\n    52â†’3. **PyTorch Trace Log:** An identical, step-by-step log from the PyTorch implementation for the same pixel.\n    53â†’\n    54â†’This allows for direct, line-by-line comparison of the entire physics calculation, making it possible to pinpoint the exact line of code where a divergence occurs.\n    55â†’### 2.2 Instrumenting the C Code\n    56â†’\n    57â†’The `nanoBragg.c` source in `golden_suite_generator/` must be instrumented with a `-dump_pixel <slow> <fast>` command-line flag. When run with this flag, the program must write a detailed log file (`<test_case_name>_C_trace.log`) containing key intermediate variables (e.g., `scattering_vector`, `h`, `k`, `l`, `F_cell`, `F_latt`, `omega_pixel`, `polar`) for the specified pixel. This provides the ground truth for component-level testing.\n    58â†’\n    59â†’### 2.3 Golden Test Cases\n    60â†’\n    61â†’The following test cases will be defined, and all three artifacts (image, C trace, PyTorch trace) will be generated and stored in `tests/golden_data/`.\n    62â†’\n    63â†’| Test Case Name | Description | Purpose |\n    64â†’| :--- | :--- | :--- |\n    65â†’| `simple_cubic` | A 100Ã… cubic cell, single wavelength, no mosaicity, no oscillation. | The \"hello world\" test for basic geometry and spot calculation. |\n    66â†’| `triclinic_P1` | A low-symmetry triclinic cell with misset orientation. | To stress-test the reciprocal space and geometry calculations. |\n    67â†’| `simple_cubic_mosaic` | The `simple_cubic` case with mosaic spread. | To test the mosaic domain implementation. |\n    68â†’| `cubic_tilted_detector` | Cubic cell with rotated and tilted detector. | To test general detector geometry implementation. |\n    69â†’\n    70â†’### 2.4 Canonical Generation Commands\n    71â†’\n    72â†’**âš ï¸ CRITICAL:** The following commands are the **single source of truth** for reproducing the golden data. It enumerates canonical commands, sweeps, thresholds, and options for the shared parity runner (`tests/test_parity_matrix.py`). Every parity-threshold AT SHALL appear in both the matrix and the YAML file.\n   242â†’\n   243â†’### 2.5.0 Bootstrap Parity Harness (blocking)\n   244â†’\n   245â†’- If either `tests/parity_cases.yaml` or `tests/test_parity_matrix.py` is missing, the matrix is incomplete. Stop before running any parity loop.\n   246â†’- Add a fix_plan item (â€œBootstrap parity harness for AT-â€¦â€) and create both files before proceeding:\n   247â†’  - `tests/test_parity_matrix.py`: parameterised pytest harness that runs the C reference (`NB_C_BIN`) and the PyTorch CLI (`sys.executable -m nanobrag_torch`), writes temporary floatfiles, loads them into NumPy, computes correlation/MSE/RMSE/maxâ€†|Î”|/sum ratio (optional SSIM), saves `metrics.json` (plus diff artifacts) on failure, and enforces thresholds specified in the YAML.\n   248â†’  - `tests/parity_cases.yaml`: a top-level `cases:` list with entries containing `id`, `description`, `base_args`, `thresholds`, optional `options`, and `runs` (array of `{name, extra_args, thresholds?}`). Include seeds and device settings when determinism demands it.\n   249â†’- After the bootstrap, rerun Step 0 so the matrix and YAML stay in sync. Parity work MUST NOT continue until both files exist and the target AT has an entry.\n   250â†’\n   251â†’### 2.5.1 Trace Recipe (per AT)\n   252â†’\n   253â†’For equivalence debugging (ATâ€‘PARALLEL failures, correlation below thresholds, structured diffs), generate aligned traces:\n   254â†’\n   255â†’- Pixel selection: choose a strong onâ€‘peak pixel close to the beam center or a specified coordinate in the test; record the exact `(s,f)` indices used.\n   256â†’- PyTorch trace: emit a structured log containing, at minimum, `pix0_vector`, basis vectors, `R` (distance), solid angle (both pointâ€‘pixel and obliquityâ€‘corrected), close_distance and obliquity factor, `k_in`, `k_out`, `S`, Miller indices (float and rounded), `F`, lattice factors (`F_latt_a/b/c`, product), `F^2`, `F_latt^2`, `omega/solid_angle`, pixel area, fluence and final intensity.\n   257â†’- C trace: run the C binary with identical parameters and print the same variables for the same pixel. If needed, add temporary printf instrumentation; keep units consistent with the PyTorch trace (meters, steradians, Ã… where noted).\n   258â†’- Dtype/device: debug in float64 on CPU for determinism unless the AT explicitly requires GPU.\n   259â†’- Artifacts: save as `reports/debug/<DATE>/AT-<ID>/{c_trace.log, py_trace.log, metrics.json, diff_heatmap.png}` and cite paths in the plan.\n   260â†’\n   261â†’### 2.5.2 Matrix Gate (hard preflight)\n   262â†’\n   263â†’Before any parity run in a debugging loop:\n   264â†’\n   265â†’- Resolve the AT in this matrix to the exact pytest node(s) and required environment.\n   266â†’- Verify `NB_C_BIN` exists and is executable; if the project uses a rootâ€‘level `./nanoBragg`, set `NB_C_BIN=./nanoBragg`.\n   267â†’- Prohibition: Do not run PyTorchâ€‘only tests first for equivalence loops. The first command MUST be the canonical Câ€‘parity pytest invocation mapped here. PyTorchâ€‘only checks are allowed only as secondary, supportive diagnostics.\n   268â†’- If an AT mapping is missing or incomplete, add a minimal entry here (test file, env, canonical command) and append a TODO in `docs/fix_plan.md` referencing the addition.\n   269â†’ - Friction rule: If the same parity steps (env export, pytest node, trace generation) are repeated across two loops, factor them into a minimal helper (e.g., a oneâ€‘liner shell alias or small script) and reference it in this matrix. Record the addition briefly in `docs/fix_plan.md` Attempts History. Do not bypass pytest; helpers should only wrap the mapped canonical commands.\n   270â†’\n   271â†’### 2.5.3 Normative Parity Coverage (SHALL)\n   272â†’\n   273â†’- Every acceptance test in `specs/spec-a-parallel.md` with a Câ†”Py numerical threshold MUST have:\n   274â†’  - A human-readable entry in this matrix (test path, environment, canonical command), and\n   275â†’  - A corresponding machine-readable case in `tests/parity_cases.yaml` powering `tests/test_parity_matrix.py`.\n   276â†’- Missing coverage in either location is blocking. The fix plan cannot mark the AT done until the mapping exists or an explicit harness entry (with pass/fail logic) is added.\n   277â†’- Documentation updates MUST keep the matrix and YAML file in sync with the canonical command line (arguments, sweeps, thresholds).\n   278â†’\n   279â†’#### 2.5.3a Parity Case Classification Criteria (SHALL)\n   280â†’\n   281â†’**Purpose:** Clarify which AT-PARALLEL tests belong in `parity_cases.yaml` (parameterized harness) vs standalone test files (custom logic).\n   282â†’\n   283â†’**Classification Rules:**\n   284â†’- **parity_cases.yaml ONLY:** Simple parameter sweeps with standard correlation/sum metrics, no custom post-processing\n   285â†’  - Examples: AT-001 (beam center scaling), AT-002 (pixel size sweeps), AT-006 (distance/wavelength sweeps)\n   286â†’- **parity_cases.yaml + Standalone (BOTH):** Basic image generation via YAML; standalone adds custom validation logic\n   287â†’  - Examples: AT-010 (adds 1/RÂ² scaling physics checks), AT-016 (adds NaN/Inf robustness checks)\n   288â†’  - Pattern: YAML generates images for correlation checks; standalone test loads those images and applies domain-specific validation\n   289â†’- **Standalone ONLY:** Custom algorithms, special infrastructure, or complex validation that cannot be expressed in YAML\n   290â†’  - Examples:\n   291â†’    - AT-008 (Hungarian peak matching algorithm)\n   292â†’    - AT-013 (deterministic mode setup, platform fingerprinting)\n   293â†’    - AT-027 (HKL file loading, FÂ² scaling validation)\n   294â†’    - AT-029 (FFT spectral analysis, aliasing measurement)\n   295â†’\n   296â†’**Linter Expectations:**\n   297â†’- The linter (`scripts/lint_parity_coverage.py`) flags all ATs with Câ†”Py correlation thresholds as potentially missing from `parity_cases.yaml`\n   298â†’- Standalone-only ATs (008, 013, 027, 029) produce warnings that should be ignored\n   299â†’- BOTH-type ATs (010, 016) should appear in parity_cases.yaml to suppress warnings; their standalone tests add extra validation\n   300â†’\n   301â†’**Decision Flowchart:**\n   302â†’1. Does the AT have a Câ†”Py correlation threshold? â†’ If NO, skip (not a parity test)\n   303â†’2. Does validation require custom Python logic (algorithms, FFT, file I/O, special checks)? â†’ If YES:\n   304â†’   - Can basic image generation use parameter sweeps? â†’ If YES, use BOTH (YAML + standalone); if NO, standalone only\n   305â†’3. Is it a pure parameter sweep with standard metrics? â†’ YES, use parity_cases.yaml only\n   306â†’\n   307â†’### 2.5.4 Artifact-Backed Closure (SHALL)\n   308â†’\n   309â†’- Success claims for parity-threshold ATs MUST cite artifacts from a mapped parity path meeting thresholds:\n   310â†’  - Metrics: correlation, MSE, RMSE, maxâ€†|Î”|, C_sum, Py_sum, sum_ratio (optional SSIM when helpful).\n   311â†’  - Storage: under `reports/<date>-AT-<ID>/metrics.json` (or equivalent) plus supporting visuals (diff heatmaps/overlays) when failures occur.\n   312â†’  - fix_plan Attempts History MUST reference these paths (look for `Metrics:` / `Artifacts:` entries).\n   313â†’- No artifacts â†’ no closure; reopen the fix plan item instead.\n   314â†’\n   315â†’### 2.5.5 Environment Canonicalization Preflight (SHALL)\n   316â†’\n   317â†’- Resolve `NB_C_BIN` before running parity commands. Preferred order: environment value â†’ `./golden_suite_generator/nanoBragg` â†’ `./nanoBragg`. Abort if none exist.\n   318â†’- Invoke PyTorch parity via `sys.executable` to ensure the active virtual environment executes the run.\n   319â†’- Treat missing binaries/interpreters as blocking errors (fail fast rather than skipping parity).\n   320â†’\n   321â†’### 2.5.6 CI Meta-Check (Docs-as-Data)\n   322â†’\n   323â†’- CI MUST lint for:\n   324â†’  - Spec â†’ matrix â†’ YAML coverage for all parity-threshold ATs.\n   325â†’  - Existence of mapped commands/binaries referenced in the YAML.\n   326â†’  - Presence of artifact paths when fix_plan marks parity items complete.\n   327â†’- CI SHOULD fail when any invariant above is violated; parity documentation is normative.\n   328â†’\n   329â†’## 2.6 CI Gates (Parity & Traces)\n   330â†’\n   331â†’To prevent drift, CI should enforce the following fast gates on CPU:\n   332â†’\n   333â†’- Detector geometry visual parity: run `scripts/verify_detector_geometry.py` and fail if any reported correlation drops below the documented thresholds (e.g., â‰¥0.999 for baseline/tilted unless otherwise specified). Save PNG and metrics JSON as artifacts.\n   334â†’- Trace parity check: generate one C trace and one PyTorch trace for the canonical pixel (`tests/golden_data/simple_cubic_pixel_trace.log` spec) and assert no firstâ€‘difference at the named checkpoints (e.g., pix0_vector, basis vectors, q, h,k,l, omega_pixel). Attach c_trace.log/py_trace.log on failure.\n   335â†’\n   336â†’Optional visual parity harness (sanity check):\n   337â†’\n   338â†’- Script: `scripts/comparison/run_parallel_visual.py`\n   339â†’- Env: `NB_C_BIN` should point to C binary\n   340â†’- Run: `python scripts/comparison/run_parallel_visual.py`\n   341â†’- Output: PNGs and `metrics.json` under `parallel_test_visuals/AT-PARALLEL-XXX/`\n   342â†’\n   343â†’When the visual harness and the AT tests disagree, treat the AT tests as the primary gate (authoritative) and use parallel traceâ€‘driven debugging (Section 2.1) to identify the first divergence. Scripts are supportive tools; conformance is determined by the pytest suite.\n   344â†’\n   345â†’## 3. Tier 1: Translation Correctness Testing\n   346â†’\n   347â†’**Goal:** To prove the PyTorch code is a faithful port of the C code.\n   348â†’\n   349â†’### 3.1 The Foundational Test: Parallel Trace Validation\n   350â†’\n   351â†’All debugging of physics discrepancies **must** begin with a parallel trace comparison. Comparing only the final output images is insufficient and can be misleading. The line-by-line comparison of intermediate variables between the C-code trace and the PyTorch trace is the only deterministic method for locating the source of an error and is the mandatory first step before attempting to debug with any other method.\n   352â†’\n   353â†’### 3.2 Unit Tests (`tests/test_utils.py`)\n   354â†’\n   355â†’**Target:** Functions in `utils/geometry.py` and `utils/physics.py`.  \n   356â†’**Methodology:** For each function, create a PyTest test using hard-coded inputs. The expected output will be taken directly from the Golden C-Code Trace Log.\n   357â†’\n   358â†’### 3.3 Component Tests (`tests/test_models.py`)\n   359â†’\n   360â†’**Target:** The `Detector` and `Crystal` classes.  \n   361â†’**Methodology:** The primary component test is the **Parallel Trace Comparison**.\n   362â†’\n   363â†’- `test_trace_equivalence`: A test that runs `scripts/debug_pixel_trace.py` to generate a new PyTorch trace and compares it numerically, line-by-line, against the corresponding Golden C-Code Trace Log. This single test validates the entire chain of component calculations.\n   364â†’\n   365â†’### 3.4 Integration Tests (`tests/test_simulator.py`)\n   366â†’\n   367â†’**Target:** The end-to-end `Simulator.run()` method.  \n   368â†’**Methodology:** For each test case, create a test that compares the final PyTorch image tensor against the golden `.bin` file using `torch.allclose`. This test should only be expected to pass after the Parallel Trace Comparison test passes.\n   369â†’\n   370â†’**Primary Validation Tool:** The main script for running end-to-end parallel validation against the C-code reference is `scripts/verify_detector_geometry.py`. This script automates the execution of both the PyTorch and C implementations, generates comparison plots, and computes quantitative correlation metrics. It relies on `scripts/c_reference_runner.py` to manage the C-code execution.\n   371â†’\n   372â†’## 4. Tier 2: Gradient Correctness Testing\n   373â†’\n   374â†’**Goal:** To prove that the automatic differentiation capabilities are mathematically correct.\n   375â†’\n   376â†’### 4.1 Gradient Checks (`tests/test_gradients.py`)\n   377â†’\n   378â†’*   **Target:** All parameters intended for refinement.\n   379â†’*   **Methodology:** We will use PyTorch's built-in numerical gradient checker, `torch.autograd.gradcheck`. For each parameter, a test will be created that:\n   380â†’    1.  Sets up a minimal, fast-to-run simulation scenario.\n   381â†’    2.  Defines a function that takes the parameter tensor as input and returns a scalar loss.\n   382â†’    3.  Calls `gradcheck` on this function and its input.\n   383â†’*   **Requirement:** The following parameters (at a minimum) must pass `gradcheck`:\n   384â†’    *   **Crystal:** `cell_a`, `cell_gamma`, `misset_rot_x`\n   385â†’    *   **Detector:** `distance_mm`, `Fbeam_mm`\n   386â†’    *   **Beam:** `lambda_A`\n   387â†’    *   **Model:** `mosaic_spread_rad`, `fluence`\n   388â†’\n   389â†’### 4.2 Multi-Tier Gradient Testing\n   390â†’\n   391â†’**Comprehensive gradient testing requires multiple levels of verification:**\n   392â†’\n   393â†’#### 4.2.1 Unit-Level Gradient Tests\n   394â†’- **Target:** Individual components like `get_rotated_real_vectors`\n   395â†’- **Purpose:** Verify gradients flow correctly through isolated functions\n   396â†’- **Example:**\n   397â†’  ```python\n   398â†’  def test_rotation_gradients():\n   399â†’      phi_start = torch.tensor(10.0, requires_grad=True, dtype=torch.float64)\n   400â†’      config = CrystalConfig(phi_start_deg=phi_start)\n   401â†’      rotated_vectors = crystal.get_rotated_real_vectors(config)\n   402â†’      assert rotated_vectors[0].requires_grad\n   403â†’      assert torch.autograd.gradcheck(lambda x: crystal.get_rotated_real_vectors(\n   404â†’          CrystalConfig(phi_start_deg=x))[0].sum(), phi_start)\n   405â†’  ```\n   406â†’\n   407â†’#### 4.2.2 Integration-Level Gradient Tests\n   408â†’- **Target:** End-to-end `Simulator.run()` method\n   409â†’- **Purpose:** Verify gradients flow through complete simulation chain\n   410â†’- **Critical:** All configuration parameters must be tensors to preserve gradient flow\n   411â†’\n   412â†’#### 4.2.3 Gradient Stability Tests\n   413â†’- **Target:** Parameter ranges and edge cases\n   414â†’- **Purpose:** Verify gradients remain stable across realistic parameter variations\n   415â†’- **Example:**\n   416â†’  ```python\n   417â†’  def test_gradient_stability():\n   418â†’      for phi_val in [0.0, 45.0, 90.0, 180.0]:\n   419â†’          phi_start = torch.tensor(phi_val, requires_grad=True, dtype=torch.float64)\n   420â†’          config = CrystalConfig(phi_start_deg=phi_start)\n   421â†’          result = simulator.run_with_config(config)\n   422â†’          assert result.requires_grad\n   423â†’  ```\n   424â†’\n   425â†’#### 4.2.4 Gradient Flow Debugging\n   426â†’- **Purpose:** Systematic approach to diagnose gradient breaks\n   427â†’- **Methodology:**\n   428â†’  1. **Isolation:** Create minimal test case with `requires_grad=True`\n   429â†’  2. **Tracing:** Check `requires_grad` at each computation step\n   430â†’  3. **Break Point Identification:** Find where gradients are lost\n   431â†’  4. **Common Causes:**\n   432â†’     - `.item()` calls on differentiable tensors (detaches from computation graph)\n   433â†’     - `torch.linspace` with tensor endpoints (known PyTorch limitation)\n   434â†’     - Manual tensor overwriting instead of functional computation\n   435â†’     - Using `.detach()` or `.numpy()` on tensors that need gradients\n   436â†’\n   437â†’## 5. Tier 3: Scientific Validation Testing\n   438â†’\n   439â†’**Goal:** To validate the model against objective physical principles, independent of the original C code.\n   440â†’\n   441â†’### 5.1 First Principles Tests (`tests/test_validation.py`)\n   442â†’\n   443â†’*   **Target:** The fundamental geometry and physics of the simulation.\n   444â†’*   **Methodology:**\n   445â†’    *   **`test_bragg_spot_position`:**\n   446â†’        1.  Configure a simple case: cubic cell, beam along Z, detector on XY plane, no rotations.\n   447â†’        2.  Analytically calculate the exact (x,y) position of a low-index reflection (e.g., (1,0,0)) using the Bragg equation and simple trigonometry.\n   448â†’        3.  Run the simulation.\n   449â†’        4.  Find the coordinates of the brightest pixel in the output image using `torch.argmax`.\n   450â†’        5.  Assert that the simulated spot position is within one pixel of the analytically calculated position.\n   451â†’    *   **`test_polarization_limits`:**\n   452â†’        1.  Configure a reflection to be at exactly 90 degrees 2-theta.\n   453â†’        2.  Run the simulation with polarization set to horizontal. Assert the spot intensity is near maximum.\n   454â†’        3.  Run again with polarization set to vertical. Assert the spot intensity is near zero.\n   455â†’\n   456â†’## 6. Tooling & Benchmark Hygiene\n   457â†’\n   458â†’- **Directory layout:** Place benchmarks, profilers, and ad-hoc tooling under `scripts/` (e.g., `scripts/benchmarks/benchmark_detailed.py`). Do not add standalone executables to the repo root.\n   459â†’- **Environment parity:** All tooling must honour the same environment contract as the tests (`KMP_DUPLICATE_LIB_OK=TRUE`, `NB_C_BIN` precedence, editable install).
